Chapter LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for certain reasons it has been read to me and I remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except for two ways: one way is so that when asked about it, the physician knows the treatment for those who need it; and the other way is that we have sometimes had a need for castration in other animals for our benefit from them, such as horses, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
Therefore, I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by cutting or by division.
In the method performed by cutting, the procedure is that we should cauterize the animal in warm water until the genitals are softened and flaccid and hang down. And then take those with your hand enclosed so that they are relaxed and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration performed by incision and division, hold the animal and press the scrotum of the testicles with your left hand.
And then lift the suspensory ligaments, and make an incision on each side so that two processes are created.
And then cut those parts after you have stripped each one. And do not leave on those of the penis any cause for injury, but rather the subtle part of the penis that is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better than the one performed by cutting, because cauterization leaves no cause from the testicles for the animal to desire copulation.
And then care for the wound until it is healed.
Chapter LXX.
On the Treatment of Hermaphrodism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: one is when it appears in the space between the scrotum of the testicles, where there is a figure resembling that of a female in which hair grows.
In some cases of that disease from which urine is discharged through a channel in the scrotum.
In women there is a special case: the female organ above the pubis is similar to the testicles of a man, slightly smaller and inward, like the scrotum of a man and two testicles.
The treatment is of three types: two for men and one type for women. It is necessary that you incise those tight tissues through which the disease escapes, and then treat them as you would other illnesses.
And in the second type for men from whom urine is discharged through a channel in the scrotum, there is no cure or surgery available.
Chapter XXI.
About hanging and flesh protrusion due to causes in women.
A mild form of hanging is naturally tight but can be stretched with careful handling; in some cases, it becomes enlarged in women to such an extent that it protrudes similarly to men and during intercourse.
Then you should grasp the excess of the hanging part with your hand or with forceps and incise it.
And do not delay in making the incision, especially at the root of the protrusion, so that it does not cause excessive bleeding.
And then treat it as you would other illnesses until it is healed.
This raw flesh is the flesh that comes out of the horrid part of the mother within which it fills up, and strongly light it is spread to the parts outside according to the appearance of a tail (and by this mostly I first called this "tailed illness"); therefore we must cut it as we would cut the navel, and treat inside so that it may be healed.
Chapter LXXII.
On the Treatment of Hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids are when the woman's hymen is not perforated, or the passage is small. And it is either natural or accidental.
It is accidental due to a previous illness, and that is caused either by loose flesh or by thin or thick phlegm.
And it is caused either in the front part of the mother, or in the sides of her, or in the upper part of her, or in the lower part of her, and it prohibits menstruation and intercourse and pregnancy, and very easily it prohibits menstruation.
And the diagnosis of that condition is made by examination with the speculum, if the obstruction is apparent, proceed directly; but if it is not apparent, then seek it out with your fingers or with a probe.
But if the obstruction is due to thin phlegm and it is close to the two lips, then you should examine and disrupt that.
And you should place cotton pads over the two lips, and then use your fingers to examine both areas carefully.
Let the woman lie on her back, spread her legs apart, and then forcefully pull both lips apart so that the small obstacle is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And immediately take some linen and soak it in oil, then place it on that area, and change it daily so that the incision does not become consolidated.
If the obstacle is large and thick, now it is necessary for you to incise that with a scalpel or with a myrtle leaf.

And immediately administer a wide lead tube so that the wound does not heal too quickly.
And hold that for several days and administer dry heat.
And immediately treat with the other method of healing until it is healed.
And in some cases, accidents occur during the natural maturation of other tissues, and at these times it is necessary to incise according to this method. But if this is due to chronic abscesses, in the case of chronic abscesses that are in the process of maturing, do not do anything contrary to them with iron in any way.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and similar conditions that occur in the genital area of women.
Hemorrhoids are an appreciation of the openings of small veins from which blood flows continuously; and with old hemorrhoids, these nodes are formed.
And now I have mentioned in the division the types of these and the signs of them, and to say also which of these receive treatment and which do not receive treatment.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and nodes when they are in the process of maturing and do not appear to the senses, at this time do not treat them with iron.
Those are the veins which are in the opening of the womb upon which one feels a touch, those are the ones that should be treated.
And when you put the woman in a bath, clean and prepare the area with scissors or with rough cloth, and cut those with the razors.
And then sprinkle on those from which the blood flows from one of the powder containers without chewing, such as acacia and similar substances.
And then press their feet for one hour, and then place that in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then have that person sit in a decoction of sumac and rind of lemons and galangal and similar substances.
And then take flour of barley and prepare that with honey and sour grape juice and make a plaster with it on her back.
And if the blood is congealed, that is good; and if not, attach to two bellows, and to the nipples without incision.
And then take wool and immerse that in the juice of cilantro or in the juice of hyssop or in the juice of garlic in sour grape juice and attach it to the place; and then treat the area with ointments until it is healed.
And treat that until it is healed.
Chapter LXXIV.
On the piercing of an abscess in the groin.
Various types of abscesses occur in the groin, such as stone and ulcerous abscesses, as well as hemorrhoids, fistulas, piles, and other abscesses. And I have already described these ailments and the types of them and the signs of them, and their treatments in the division.
And what I say in this treatise about abscesses refers to those that occur in the groin when they are infected, and if you want to know how the operation is performed.
Then you should consider whether the pain of the abscess at its beginning is sharp with percussion and phlegm and fever, and if it appears red and feels painful when touched, then do not proceed with piercing it, and treat it in such a way that helps with maturation until the acute symptoms subside.
And now you should have the woman lie on a chair that has two arms; she should recline on her back and position her legs with her feet below the abdomen, and spread her thighs apart, and place her arms below her elbows, and bind them with bandages as appropriate.
And then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the groin will be made, the form of which will be described in these cases.
And when you want to administer this instrument, you should place it along the edge of the abscess in the woman's groin, and what is inserted from the instrument into the groin should not exceed the length of the abscess itself. If the instrument is larger than the opening of the greatest orifice, then at that time you must apply poultices to the tissue around the greatest orifice so that no part of the instrument enters the greatest orifice.
And you must place the lubricant that flows from the instrument of the back above it, and the minister should hold the instrument while turning the lubricant inside until the opening of the greatest orifice is sufficiently moistened.
And when the wound appears and is touched with the hand and feels hot and moist, then at that time you must dry it by applying a powder to the head of the wound.
And when the pus is evacuated, then you must apply to the wound a piece of cloth immersed in rose oil or green oil, which has some astringent properties; and place a plaster on the dry section around the wound.
And place clean wool over the greatest orifice and on top of it, place lamb's wool immersed in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And it should be treated appropriately for about two days until you find the method that suits this condition until it is healed.
And sometimes the greatest orifice and the wound should be washed in this way with water and honey, and sometimes with water in which the root of lily or long-leaved arum has been boiled, and then return to the appropriate treatment.
And if the wound is deep within a swollen orifice, then you must be cautious about treating it with metal instruments; instead, treat it as we have described in the division.
Chapter LXXV.
To teach midwives in what manner living embryos are treated when it appears unnatural according to figure.
A necessary cause is that the midwife knows at the beginning the figure of normal childbirth by signs of light, and it is when you see the woman pressing down below and desiring to breathe air, and she is deceived by what is above her during labor, then you know that this birth is according to natural figure, and the delivery is over the head, and in the second one either hanging from or suspended by the navel.
When you see those signs, then it is appropriate to compress the abdomen so that the embryo descends lightly because when it is delivered over its head, the second one will be delivered, and these are cleansed by proper cleansing.
But that which is different from this birth is unnatural and blame-worthy, for when the embryo is delivered on its feet and the body of it is delivered before its head and feet, or one hand or foot first, or the head and a hand or foot, or the belly, and easily turns over its neck, resembling the figures that are blame-worthy.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all those matters, and to guard against error and deception.
And I show all the figures of those cases, and which condition is in them so that it may be signified by that and remain on that.
When the fetus is delivered over its head by natural effort, and that is strenuous for the woman and makes childbirth difficult, and you see the strength of hers already diminished, then make her drink, or let the women hold her, and evaporate the sweat from her using fenugreek powder and moist oils.
Then insert the probe between the said small spaces and split it with the second instrument, or open it with its nail until you remove what is inside from humidity. And press the woman's abdomen so that the contents come out.
But if it does not come out, now cover the woman with a mixture of finely ground wheat and fenugreek seeds mixed together.
Then tell him, after the cleansing, to be made to sneeze with certain conditions; and do this at his mouth and nose for one hour, because the contents will be expelled immediately.
And if both parts of the contents are expelled at the beginning, now you should reduce them to small pieces little by little. But if he does not obey the instrument, now place the woman on a cushion and lift her off it, and then strike the cushion on the ground; and hold the woman so that she does not fall due to the striking.
And if the parts are not returned inside and the contents rot, now incise them and extract the remaining contents or tie his hand to a cloth and pull it out with equality, because it will be expelled.
When the contents are on the membranes, now you should push them up, and then compress the contents gently, and then even them out, and then take a piece of it and stretch them little by little.
When pus has settled inside the abscess, then you order him to squeeze it out in convenient times, for it will come out if God so wills.
And if it does not come out as we have recommended, then you return the operation little by little until you stop at the second figure of nature, for it will now come out easily and quickly.
And if it is prohibited by all that we have recommended, then take musellage of hartshorn and dissolved gum, and pound it all in the mortar with good pounding, and afterwards apply it to the place where the woman's womb feels pain, below her navel. And then have the patient sit in hot water, so that it reaches the hypochondria.
And when the parts below his armpits are cleansed, then you perform the smoking with myrtle and have him undergo that. And when the smoking lasts for one hour, then you have him sit on a chair, and afterwards make him sneeze and open his mouth, and remove that, and press the part below his navel gently, for the matter will soon come out.
Insert the finger laterally during the expulsion of the matter. Be skillful in reducing the hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and let it go.
And if it cannot be let go, then make her lie down on the bed, and strike her body vigorously with blows, and then administer liniments which are cool and composed of mucilaginous substances.
And if labor has begun, then make her sit on the birth stool, and then proceed with the reduction of the hand, and massage the matter out according to its natural shape, and make the woman sneeze and instruct her to exert herself until it is expelled.
Insert the finger over the shoulder using your fingers and the strap to guide it, with the mother lying on her side. Let the midwife hold the hand of the fetus and then turn it little by little, so that it may be facilitated.
And when and how it is massaged, then pause on the area that we have recommended with oil and mucilaginous substances.

When deciding on the horror of the major according to this method, consider it, and then you incise with your fingernail so that it is evacuated of the humidity.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of it, then you incise at that part of the belly, so that it is not retained and dies.

The exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins usually are born in a single birth, and sometimes three or four [are born], but this is rare and uncommon; however, these cases are due to causes other than nature, and they do not occur often.
And with those [twins], whether they are multiple, make one incision, and separate them by a suture, distinguishing each along the umbilical cord. Sometimes they are expelled in such a way that it seems like a single fetus is being born naturally, while at other times they are expelled improperly as we have recounted.

A reminder of what is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus as we have said in the division of the treatment and it does not come out, then you must use surgical intervention. At this time, it is necessary to consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and not suffering from any of the conditions for which her safety is feared.
Now the woman should be placed on her back on the bed with her buttocks raised and her head tilted downwards.
And the attendant should hold her by both legs or tie her to the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then moisten the mouth of the mother with olive oil and mucus made from honey, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucus, and then gently inserts her hand into the mother, and then searches with her hand for the location where the hooks are in the fetus.
In suitable places: then you consider whether the poultice is prepared to be placed over the patient's head, and at that time you place the hooks in the ears of the patient, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or under the beard, or in the clavicle, or in the proper places of the ribs, or under the hypochondria.
If the poultice is to be placed on the patient's feet, then place it in the heel, or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary that you hold the hook with your right hand, and place the curvature of it in the place between the fingers of your left hand, and insert it with ease into one of those places which we have mentioned, until it reaches the affected area.
And then place and fix in position another hook, or a third if necessary, so that there is an equal pull, and not an extension according to its straightness alone.
And it should be gentle in all parts, so that the extraction of it is eased just as it is done in the teeth for their extraction.
And it is necessary in the area between them that the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them carefully and manipulate what is retained.
Then if a part of the fetus is protruded, at that time the hooks should be moved to the place which is more prominent; and do this until all of the fetus is delivered.
If the hand is dislocated against another part and it is not possible to reduce it by contortion, then at this point a cloth must be wrapped around it; and after that extract it until all is dislodged, and incise it either in the joint of the hand or in the elbow.
And do this also with the other hand and with both feet.
But if the head of the boil is large, or happens in the contortion when it is dislocated, or at the head of the tight bandage, then you should insert between the said spines and cut open the head and drain the fluid, or expose that part with an instrument called “alundat,” the form of which will be among the forms of other instruments in the chapter close to this one.
And similarly do if the boil has a large head by nature: then you should incise that with some instrument, or take it as we have said using an alundat; and then extract the contents from the bones with forceps.
And if the head is dislocated and contorted behind the clavicle, then it should be cut open so that the moisture which is in the tissues can be drained.
But if it is not complicated and does not adhere to the dislocation, then you should incise the head as soon as it is possible for you.
And if the lower part of the abdomen is abscessed or affected by dropsy, then you should puncture it so that the moisture which is inside can drain.
But if the boil is on the legs, then the attraction of it is distant and the direction toward the mouth of the vein is distant.
If it is necessary to open the belly and the thighs, at that time you should take out the cloth with which you have wrapped your hand, and cut open the belly and the thighs so that the fluid within them can run out.
If the other members remain stiff and turn the head, then place your left hand in between; but if the mother's mouth is open, then insert your hand into her throat, and grasp with it the head, and pull those mentioned into the mother's mouth, and immediately insert an inch or two inches, and pull them along with that.
And if the mother's mouth is obstructed by an abscess or boil that occurs on it, then it should not be bandaged over it; instead, at that time apply moist and fatty applications. And apply plasters; and follow with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, make it lie down; and administer what we have said about a living birth.
And if this is not possible, then cut it into pieces and extract it.
And make sure that you do not leave any cause inside the secondine.
And when you have completed all of your operation, then administer what we have said about the treatment for abscesses that occur to the mother.
And if bleeding occurs, then apply styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
I have seen a woman in whose womb was a dead fetus, and above that another pregnancy, and the other fetus was also dead. It happened to one after a long time that an abscess formed in the place of pregnancy; and it inflated inside where the fetus was, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time, but the illness did not improve.
Then I applied some causes of strong attraction to her and extracted one bone from her, and after passing several days, I extracted another bone; and I was very surprised, as there were no bones in the womb.
And then I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I questioned the illness and extracted many bones from her, the woman existing in her usual state, and thus treated her for a long time, until she discharged a little pus.
And I did not find it strange, but rather realized that in this way there is knowledge and assistance for what the physician uses his hands to administer in treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of a spiral in which the largest part is at the top:
This is the form of a stretcher on which the leaves are balanced, to which there are two spirals at the ends of two posts. However, may this virtue be such that it is more subtle than a thread, and let it be made either of wool or of the wood of a tree.
And let the width of each piece be two fingers, and the margin on each side be one finger; and the length of each should be half a palm plus a bit more, and at the middle point between two pieces, attach therefrom those same wooden fittings which are already fixed, whose length is about half a palm plus a little more, and the width of each is two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions should be inserted into the mouth of the larger one so that they are open to them when you rotate the two prescribed threads.
Form another similar one that is even finer and lighter:
Let it be made of wood or tree bark, according to the likeness of forceps. However, at the end of those two additions as you see fit, and the length of those additions is about one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the larger one, then you have her lie on the bed with her feet hanging down, open that which is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with scissors equally according to the amount you want, within the opening of the larger one until the metrona does what you want.

Form of expelling what is expelled:
Form of joining what contains the great head

Form of one having two spines:
Form of a spatum having two extremities at which the head is divided:
Form of two broad spatulae:
All those instruments are exercised, and when their various types are multiplied and prepared by the artisans, it becomes easier for them to perform their operations and they become more useful for people in proportion to their quantity.
And you must prepare yourself for the use of those instruments, wherever they may be needed, for the necessity of them is inexcusable.
Of the extraction of the second one.
When the second birth is retained during childbirth, you must command the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze under certain conditions. Place your hand over her mouth and nose, and if this causes it to come out as a result, that is good.
Take some wool and at this time take a piece of it and pierce through its covering a hole and place in that herbs to fill the mouth of the wound, such as calamint and rue and anise and chamomile and Arabic saffron and cinnamon and sage. All of these herbs or some of them should be immersed in water in the wool, and place that over the fire.
And then place a reed tube in the mouth of the wound, and keep it there until the vapor reaches the cavity of the wound.
And then make the person sneeze as we have said, and the second time let it be expelled quickly.
But if it remains close to this treatment and is not expelled, then you order the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or almond oil, and then insert that into the cavity and search with that for the second object. And when you have found it, then take it out little by little. But if it is stuck in the root of the wound, then insert her hand as we have recommended, and when she has found the second object, extract it slowly so that the patient does not fall due to strong attraction. Also make sure that it alternates between the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the wound is obstructed, we have already recommended the treatment through sneezing and the medication of the wool with herbs.
If it is not expelled along with all the causes that we have recounted, then be careful not to over-exert in repeated attempts at abstraction. But instead ensure that what remains inside goes from the mouth of the mother into the body of the woman, and subsequently apply a pessary for finding and expelling; for this will cause it to pass after some days and it will dissolve and be expelled.
When it is passed, raise the woman's head and place it above her chest and stomach, which will alleviate the illness; then it is necessary to administer fumigations and appropriate treatments for this.
However, some of the Ancients were accustomed to administer fumigation with natrtle and dried figs.
Form of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated due to retention of menstruation and dysmenorrhea:
It should be made of wood or ivory.
And the narrow end should be placed in the vagina and the wide end above the fire, and the fumigation should be placed on the coals of the fire.
And keep that inside until the fumigation is completely consumed and repeat it with another one.
Treatment for the uncircumcised penis of a child.
Some children are born with uncircumcised penises, which become tight and covered. Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that foreskin with her fingernail; and if not, pierce it with a sharp probe, but be careful not to touch the glans.
About the flax soaked in wine and oil; and then treat that which is found within until it is clean.
If you fear that it is obstructed, then for a few days apply a tube made of cloth, and remove it when the child wishes to vomit.
And if constipation of the anus occurs due to consolidation of an abscess or swelling; then it must be that this consolidation be incised, and afterward it should be treated with what we have said about treatment and lead.
On the treatment of fistulas that occur below.
Fistulas that occur in the lower region, near the base and thick in nature, which appear near the anus outside or in the space between one part.
And it is either one fistula or multiple.
And as this swelling becomes old and drains watery or white mucus or subtle pus, and some of these fistulas are penetrating.
And these penetrating ones are known by what comes out of them through drainage and swelling; and sometimes the condition of drainage is bad, and it is easily recognized as such.
And some of these fistulas extend in the space penetrating into the bladder and into the urethra; and some penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the bone of the leg.
And to distinguish a penetrating fistula from a non-penetrating one near the anus, you should insert your finger into the anus, and gently introduce a thin probe of iron or metal into the fistula when there is no turbulence.
If there is pus in that place, then insert a fine probe of lead or horsehair so that you can feel the probe or hair with your finger.
And if you do not feel any of that and do not find any cause for evacuation, whether worms or gas, as we have said, then you know it is non-penetrating, and at that point apply yourself to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urethra, then the treatment consists in this manner of urine from that and prohibits doing so that the affected area may be consolidated by medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the joint of the spine or into the bone and there is pain in the circumference, then the sign of this is that the probe passes here if there is no pus around the bone, and there is pain in the circumference of the affected area; and you will have lasting weakness from it; and that it cannot be treated with medicine, nor is it consolidated by encounter.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the treatment of these is laborious and futile for physicians, as that is their firm belief.
But in the one that is not penetrating and is not chronic, healing with proper treatment is hoped for, as I will now recommend to you, and what has already been beneficial.
And it is that the patient lies down on their back with their legs raised up and the spine inclined towards the abdomen, and then insert a probe of lead or iron if there is pus in the fistula, so that you can feel where the probe goes.
And if the patient complains of pain around the anus, then you must insert your finger into the anus.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe easily penetrates, or if you feel something between your finger and the membrane or flesh, then you will certainly know that it has penetrated; and do not work on this, because there is no cure in this case, as we have said.
But if someone were to say that it heals in some men slowly.
And concerning the treatment by which improvement is hoped for, you should ignite a cautery gently according to the width of the fistula, as was previously described, and insert that heated instrument into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those inflamed tissues are now constricted like the quill of a bird.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in butter until all those constricted tissues heal, and afterward treat it with medicines that promote and consolidate tissue growth. If it heals, that is good; but if not, then it will never heal by any other treatment.
And if the probe enters but does not penetrate beyond your finger that is in the anus, and between it and the probe there is a thin layer of flesh or membrane, and sometimes the fistula ends on the surface of the buttock, then dry the area from the beginning of the fistula, and you will see the drying reach to where the tip of the probe reaches, and by this method it is freed and cured.
And clean the flesh of those fistulas which are like an owl’s feather tube and do not cut any part for that reason.
But if blood flows frequently between you and your operation when you incise those tissues, then quickly it should be done, and for the pus a sharp instrument is to cauterize with fire or with an acute medicine, because cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: one is the adjustment of those tissues adjusted, and the other is the absorption of blood and the drying up of humidity.
And then treat that which is wrapped in bandages or cloth three times a day until the place sweats, and then quickly treat the plague with hard flesh-forming applications that generate and consolidate.
And for medicines in which there is styptic and drying properties; when they are restored, it is healed and you do not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula has already penetrated into the anal region and is long from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
And thus if you find the fistula and between you and it is a membranous or flesh barrier, and it is prone to penetration, then there should be no operation but rather proceed by faith and hope.
The cause should be administered in one of three ways: either cauterize it as we have said; or dry it until you achieve the firmness necessary for you to insert certain instruments and begin treatment properly; do not proceed with drying if it does not allow access to the pus, and ensure that the patient is informed about this process without causing distress; then treat it as we have said because it will heal easily. Or extend that membrane and clean the pus that dries out close to the anus, as we have said, or use a probe or another sharp instrument, and then cleanse those fistulated tissues which are revealed in the section; afterward, strive to restore the entire wound through drying, and if the upper opening does not consolidate, leave the open fistula on the side of the anus, and it will be easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is treated in this manner: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the crack of the buttocks around the surface of the body near the thigh and on the edge of the buttock, then take out the probe from its perforated tip, which is like a needle for preparing the hearts according to this form:
and insert into that vein wrapped around it with five veins or so; then immediately insert the probe into the vein in the fistula until you reach the curvature of it.

Regarding the stitching of hemorrhoids in which blood flows during the incision of those areas.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds, one kind in the region near the anus similar to those that are like coal, or those which are like radish flesh. And of those there are small and large ones, and the blood flows from them constantly and they are one type, and they are mobile, and they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are due to little moisture, from which yellowish water or a little bloody mucus flows continuously, and their appearance depends on the color of the skin.
And the treatment for those that are inside the anus is to command the patient to sit down and compress the area until the anus opens and the hemorrhoids become visible to you. Then you cover yourself and suspend with hooks or what you have with your nail, and then cut those away from their roots.
However, if you do not have hooks because of the moisture and softness of those hemorrhoids, then take a rough cloth or a comb or a piece of wool, and extract those with your fingers, and then cut them and powder should be sprinkled near the incision to serve as a cauterizing agent; or cauterize them as previously described in the chapter on cauterization. And then treat those with other methods until they are healed.
And if the anus does not respond to evacuation, then apply a small bite of a blister to the patient using water that is in the anus so that it facilitates quick evacuation when the patient strains.
If the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of theirs is lightness, and it is that you take those with your finger, or that you take those with ointment, and incise those, and afterwards cure those with what we have said within until they are healed.
And for the one whom you have incised, see that you manage sutures of theirs according to this manner: take thread wrapped and insert that in needle and then extract the hemorrhoids at the top parts, and make that penetrate with the needle into the flesh on the other side, and wrap both ends of the thread at the part below the needle, and so horizontally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with a strong structure, and then tie off the thread and extract the needle.
And do this for all of them, and leave one of those unsewn, so that the excess blood can flow from that one.
And then place over the anus a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax; and place that on it and command the patient to rest. And then leave that inside until it heals; and when it is healed, cure those with baths or with other treatment until they are healed.
And when they become chronic and do not respond to that medicine, then you should scrape those with the point of a scalpel or with your finger until they are made moist and the scab above them is removed, which prevents their consolidation; and then treat them until they are healed.

Of the treatment of plagues.
I have already stated in the division of the treatment of plagues what was appropriate for the book, and I will now describe the treatment of those with medicine according to the regimen.
Therefore, I say that plagues are diverse according to what causes the plagues and according to the place where the plague occurs.
And the causes by which wounds leading to plagues occur are such as stone embedding, or cutting by a sword or knife, or striking with a lance, or with a staff, or with an arrow, or similar to those from various causes.
Here are the plagues that occur in the parts of the body, such as a plague that affects the head, neck, feet, abdomen, groin, and similar ones in the limbs.
And I also recommend the treatment of certain plagues, so that you pause that reasoning and rule regarding other plagues.
And I will begin with the simple plagues of the head, for the recall of the compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs on the head and it is not a fracture, you should consider: if it is due to a blow from a stone or similar object, and if only the skin has been broken but it is a large wound and you fear that an abscess might form there, then you must take action immediately and perform bloodletting on the cephalic vein without delay; do not postpone this. And extract as much blood as necessary according to the quantity required by its strength, unless some cause prohibits bloodletting, especially if little blood has come out of the wound.
And let the bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part; and protect the patient from overeating and from eating heavy foods.
But if some reason prevents you from bloodletting, then reduce the patient's food intake and do not allow them to eat meat or rich foods.
And treat the plague with care if an abscess forms, applying it only in rose oil or in wine that has been stypticized.
But if you are certain of an abscess forming, then treat the wound if it is fresh and the air has not yet changed the powder that I recommend to be applied in small amounts.
And if the air has already changed that, then pause for some time until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or due to a fracture and the lips of it are not suitable for stitching together, then stitch those as I will explain regarding the suture of such wounds.
But if the wound is already exposed from the bone and flesh and there is no need to hold it back except for a small suspensorium, then incise that and immediately treat the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in place of stitches, and instruct the patient to eat food that is light: eggs, fish, and similar foods until he is healed.
And if you find that the stitches have become putrid and do not adhere to the bone, then cut out all of that decayed material and remove it, and subsequently treat it.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which bleeding may occur and it does not stop with medicines, then press on the artery. If you find that it has not stopped bleeding, then cut it with a scalpel or ligate it; and if necessity compels you and what we have said does not suffice, then cauterize until the bleeding stops.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is minor; sprinkle this powder on them, for it will consolidate those wounds before the air changes them.
And the method for making the powder is as follows: take oil of sesame one part, dragon's blood two parts, and burnt frankincense three parts; mix them thoroughly and sift, then fill the wound with this mixture, and compress it properly so that it adheres well to the wound, and let it coagulate with the blood.
From the depth of the wound above apply poultices and leave them on without removing them while it is still such that it has not formed an abscess, for medicine does not reach it until it is healed.
And sometimes this cure is used alone when it is not at hand, the juice and blood of a dragon.
And this method of operation is used for large wounds when it is necessary to place them open and narrow, and for fresh wounds with their blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, especially when it is in summer time, then do not apply the position of this powder, but at that time cure them with what we have said, by placing on those some cooling digestive herbs, or place on those flour dust mixed with water and honey until they begin to rot; and afterward cure them with the other treatment until they are healed.
But if it happens with the wound that there is a fracture in the bone, and it is small, then you extract it with forceps.

Of wounds to the neck.

But if the wound has already penetrated into the bone, then probe it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all that you can; and what is not accessible to you, leave it until the wound suppurates, and the excretion from it subsides.

If there is a thrust wound from a spear or knife, and if you examine its depth, then consider whether the wound produces swelling when the injured person moves; at this point, you will know that the wound is fatal.
And if there is no depth to it and the wound is recent with fresh blood, then apply powder for the first hour, and do not press on it so that the blood does not remain trapped in its depth and return to the heart, causing further injury; rather, apply an attractive ointment, and change this twice a day.
And if the ointment is not available to you, then place a piece of cloth on the wound opening so that it absorbs any moisture; and have the injured person lie on the wound so that what is trapped in it flows out.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound occurred and no spasms, tremors of the heart, or constriction of the limbs has affected the injured person, and you observe other good signs from it, then you know that the wound is safe; at this point, treat it with dressings and other healing methods until it is healed.
But if healing of it is unnecessary and the area has remained open for some time, then you know that a fistula has formed; treat it therefore according to its chapter.
And if the wound is from a spear or knife, and it is simple on the surface of the skin or flesh, then treat it as you would with stitching if it is large, or with powder if it is small.
If there has already been a probe inserted into the bone, and some pieces were cut off with it, then you should rotate the wound to try to extract those pieces if they are separate. But if they are not separate, then leave them inside until the wound heals, as their removal would be easier.

For wounds of the abdomen.
The condition that occurs in the abdomen is either severe, slight, or moderate.
A small disruption is difficult to manage by other methods, and it is also harder to return them to their proper place if you do not promptly address the intrusion back to its location, as it swells and becomes enlarged, making instruments difficult to use.
Therefore, the best condition is moderate, as in this case it is not difficult to return the bowel to its place, unlike in the two extreme cases mentioned earlier.
And you should know that there are four methods of stitching the abdomen, but two of these methods are common and suitable for stitching other wounds on the body.
Of two other sutures proper communicate with other wounds, but however more in the suture of the abdomen.
And I recommend to you each exposition and declaration.
Thus I say that when the wound is small and it becomes compressed by some cause of the bowel through it, and it becomes difficult to reduce it, then this happens in one of two ways: either due to the smallness of the rupture as we have said, or when inflammation occurs in the bowel due to the coldness of the air.
And thus when this is so, then it is necessary that you warm it in such a way that you submerge a sponge or cloth soaked in lukewarm water alone, or steeped in warm water with cyperus and spica, and apply it to the bowel until the inflammation is resolved.
And sometimes I use that which has styptic properties, and it is better than water alone in resolving the inflammation.
And thus when you see the inflammation resolved, then you moisten the bowel with water in which tea and mallows have been steeped, for by this the instrument is made smooth with little irritation.
But if the instrument is irritated near this treatment, then you should divide the rupture slightly with an instrument on which hemorrhoids have been divided.
And the first treatment is better, when it is appropriate that there be no cutting, and there should be no need to dry out due to necessity and deficiency.
Concerning the instrument, here is its form:
One part of the sharp edge of the probe, and the other part not sharp, and the tip subtle, and not as fine as a needle, but slightly blunt.
And so when the wound is enlarged and the edges are separated from the fascia, it is now necessary that its reduction be according to its natural form in its proper place, if possible in this manner, for it is better.
But when the disruption is wide and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, now you must make the patient lie on his back, and place his arms further from his head than his own head; and if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then you place his head and feet higher than the middle parts.
And similarly, if the disruption is in one of the two sides of the abdomen, now direct your attention and consideration constantly so that the side in which the wound is lies higher than the other.
And so you must administer this for both large wounds and medium-sized wounds.
And for small wounds, prepare what is necessary, and then have one of your most skilled assistants perform the task, who should hold the wound with their hand and align the edges, and then proceed to suture it appropriately.
And this is the common method of suturing: take a needle, or an equivalent needle according to the quantity and amplitude of the wound; then place the tip of the needle at the end of the disruption from the middle finger, and pull the needle tight enough so that you do not place stitches at both ends of the suture, but rather between two points inside the edges of the wound; and once you have joined the two ends of the suture and the two points inside the edges, this makes four knots.
About the length of a finger, make a double loop around the needle, and take several turns on both sides, then bring together the two lips and the wound by decent joining; then lay the thickness of a finger and put another needle in that one, then tie that loop as you did with the first needle; and do not stop doing this if it is necessary with the needles until you have completed all the stitching of the wound.
And the needles should be of medium size between coarseness and fineness, for fine needles penetrate the flesh quickly; and coarse ones are difficult to insert in the tissue, and therefore it is desirable that they be of medium size in terms of both fineness and thickness.
And it is not advisable to place the needle at both ends of the tissue in a straight line, because this causes the flesh to be cut quickly and the wound may separate before it has consolidated.
And do not extend the stitches too far apart so that the wound is not hindered from consolidating.
And then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping; and place loose powders around the stitches, which should cover the ends of the needles; and leave them until you know that the wound has already consolidated.
And this type of stitching with needles is most convenient for small wounds, as it suffices to use one or two needles or around that number.
But the second type of stitching is more common: it involves managing all four ends, of the tissue and two ends of the suture thread, at once, with a needle that is properly wrapped in terms of both fineness and thickness.
When you have pierced these four extremities with the needle, withdraw the needle from that middle part from which you started, so that the thread can be drawn up to the most prominent part of the wound, so that the suture may lie like a cloth stitch upon the cloth where the edges are stretched tight.
And pause between each suture by the amount of the thickness of the little finger.
And this suture is known to the people.
And in such a suture I closed the wound which had been inflicted on a man's abdomen with a knife, and the tearing of the wound was more than one palm wide, and it was situated around two palms from the midgut vessel, and the tearing was at the center of the limb; then I closed that after the gut had protruded from the wound for twenty-four hours.
And the wound healed in the space of fifteen days or so, and I treated him and he was cured; and after that he spoke for some time, and returned to his normal condition.

On the treatment of boil and fistula.
Know that every wound and abscess when it invilifies and becomes old, and turns into an ulcer, and is not consolidated even after a long time and has not been excised, whether in any limb, is universally called fistula, and we refer to it as such a boil.
And truly, a fistula is a felted knot, hard and white, at which there is no pain but to which there is attraction as there is attraction for birdlime; and because of this it is called a sticky boil, that is, a trap.
And in some people, it is moist, which lasts for a long time; and the moisture is excised within a few hours in others. In some cases, this moisture is moved, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
I have now shown all those causes, and the signs of them, and the cure for them with medicine in the division.
And it is appropriate that I tell you about the treatment of fistulas, which is performed through surgery with my methods.
And you should know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; among them are fistulas that extend to large veins and arteries, or nerves, or the bladder, or the intestines, or the bladder, or one of the ribs, or one of the vertebrae of the back, or one of the compound joints composed similarly to the wrist and ankle; and some of these affect parts close to major limbs and similar areas.
And therefore, among these fistulas that follow this method, they are diseases difficult to heal, and do not easily receive a cure, and treating them requires effort and ignorance.
And if any of the fistulas has a depth that does not reach the places mentioned above and you hope for and trust in its cure and wish to ascertain knowledge of it, then take a probe of iron or steel, and if the fistula runs straight ahead, explore it with this.
And if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe made of thin lead, for the lightness of its body causes it to float and bend around the tortuosity.
And if the fistula has openings that are frightening, it is not within your power to signify upon them with a probe.
Then irrigate the openings through those openings, for the moisture with which you irrigate will reach the other openings and flow out from them.
And then inquire very carefully according to the method by which you can know whether here are bones or nerves, and whether the depth of the fistula is distant or near, or if it is a fistula with multiple openings that lies above all this within your power, within your examination, in which you examine the disease, and the cause of the pain under your compression on the place, and similar signs and accidental causes related to the abscess.
And when you have stood on all those causes with true observation, then proceed to the treatment according to your confidence: and that is that you now consider whether it is an apparent fistula near or in a salt place, distant from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places I have told you about.
Now you should dry the fistula according to what was said earlier about its description, and remove what is in that filtration and of corrupted flesh, and what has grown in the opening of the flesh or of similar tissue, and treat it until it is healed.
If the fistula is of great depth and runs straight, it is necessary to incise that as deeply as you can, and then remove all corrupted flesh; afterwards apply hot applications wrapped in sharp medicines, and insert them into the cavity of the fistula which you have probed with iron.
And do this several times until the sharp medicine has dissolved everything that remains in the cavity of the fistula from corruption.
And then treat it with applications that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
But if it does not heal with this treatment, then you should cauterize it as we have recommended.
But if the cause of the fistula is bone and you must determine this, then you should probe it and dry it as we have recommended, unless you find any reason to avoid doing so because of a vein, nerve, or major limb as we have said.
But if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness on it, then you should scrape that until all the corruption is removed; afterwards treat it with substances that promote flesh growth until it heals.
And if it does not heal and pus continues to discharge as before, then you will know that you have not completely eradicated the corruption; therefore, uncover it again and carefully examine and clean it thoroughly with your strongest means, and then treat it.
And if it heals, that is good; but if not, then you will know that the corruption is in the deep recesses of the body, which you have not reached, and thus in that case there is nothing for you to do but to let nature take its course.
And if the corrupted bone is small, it is up to you to remove that; then you pull it out with fine forceps which are suitable for this purpose.
And if there are many bones, then carefully perform the extraction of all of them, and do not leave any because of your strength.
But if any cause of moisture hinders you, and in their incision there is no fear or error, then incise those ligaments or muscles as necessary, and release the bones.
But if you do not have the preparation to remove the bones at this time, then apply something that can reduce the swelling to the affected area, and leave it there until it is surrounded by flesh and ligaments. Protect the area so that it does not become consolidated, and ensure that the section you incised during your operation remains open.
Having said that, if you are concerned, apply a poultice submerged in hot salted oil or a poultice submerged in Egyptian ointment, or one of the green ointments, because when these will reduce those ligaments, and the bones are separated from their attachment, and the attraction is alleviated.
But if it is a large bone such as the bone of a camel or cow or similar, and what is corrupted on it is only the surface, then scrape off that corruption with a tool only behind where the blackness and corruption are, and then restore the wound.
But if what is corrupted is a large part of it, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to close that area and thoroughly incise it where the corruption has spread, and then treat it until it is healed and consolidated.
Here is what is recommended for you concerning the treatment of a person in their condition so that you may follow this example and assist with your operation.
A young man around xxx years old experienced pain in his body, and the part inside where the matter is located within the body has become infected, resulting in a large abscess, and it is not due to an external cause.
Then time was wasted due to the doctors' error until the abscess became severe, and pus formed from the matter, and his treatment was delayed until an opening had to be made in the abscess, and openings were created for the pus and the moisture of the body to drain.
Then many doctors treated him for two years, and none of them had knowledge in the art until I was called.
I saw the abscess and the matter flowing from those openings in large quantities; his body was completely weakened, and his complexion was yellowish.
Then I inserted a probe into one of those openings and the probe reached the bone.
Then I quickly examined all the openings and found that they reached all parts of the abscess.
Then I decided to incise one of the openings so that I could expose part of the bone, and found it to be corrupted; it was already turned to earth and decayed, and part of the abscess had penetrated into the marrow.
And then I used what was shown to me and prepared from the exposed bone.
And I cut out not from the bone but that corruption which I had previously identified and prepared to remove.
And then I paused the treatment of the wound with consolidative medicine for a long time, and it did not heal.
And then I repeated and exposed further on the bone secondly over the initial exposure, and found continuing corruption in the bone.
And I removed what appeared to me from that corruption, and then I was compelled to perform the cure of it and its restoration, and it did not restore.
And then I exposed another part and did not stop incising the bone little by little particularly to restore it, and it did not heal until I had cut around one palm's width of it, and that extracted along with its marrow, and then I restored that with medicines, and it healed quickly and was cured.
And it is not necessary to repeat the operation and cutting of it except for the disposition of its fever and the lack of its tolerance and fear of death, because it was afflicted at all hours due to excessive evacuation of syncope malaise.
And thus it healed completely, and there is no flesh instead of the hard bone; and his condition improved in his body, and he regained his strength; and he returned to his normal state and did not experience contrary effects during movement or harm from any cause.

On the treatment of hemorrhoids and the quality of enemas with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess extends inward until it collects pus, and then it ruptures and is perforated, and the pus is discharged from it, leaving the place empty as if it were a vessel, and the membrane above it remains thin like cloth, and has not reached corruption, nor does it affect bone or nerve or tendon, it is called a hemorrhoid, and it is not named a fistula.
However, if the space extends inward such that corruption affects some member, it is then called a fistula and not a hemorrhoid.
And in the treatment of which incise that scab exactly as it is turned over, and especially when it has become fine like cloth, and make sure that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the scab will adhere and that such corruption has not yet succeeded by later consequence, and on the scab there has passed some time facing up, then now treat it with an enema.
And when you consider the sinus, and now if it is large, and the arm that you use smells foul, then administer an enema with Egyptian medicine consisting of oil, vinegar, and turpentine in equal parts, and mix them in a vessel until the medicine becomes thick like honey.
And then take what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; and administer the enema to the sinus, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine inside for the duration of two hours.
And then extract that enema with care; and do this for several days until the sinus is cleansed and the odor is removed.
And at times an enema is given with ash water when this medicine is not available to you; and take the ashes of herbs, put them over the water; then strain it and administer that enema until you are confident that the sinus is now cleansed.
And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then administer an enema with water and honey mixed thoroughly, and give an enema of vinegar and honey mixed together, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and vinegar helps the sinus adhere, especially when the vinegar is rich in astringency and dryness.
And when you wash certain areas and feel that the sinus has been drained, then irrigate it with water that promotes the growth of flesh.
And it is that you should take a decoction of dry ingredients and dissolve them in rose oil and vinegar; or what you irrigate it with certain medicines and other decoctions which have the properties that I have already written about in the chapter on decoctions.
And if the opening of the sinus is narrow and does not receive the tube for irrigation, then gradually enlarge it with a small instrument, and place in it a plug wrapped in Egyptian decoction or basilicon decoction until it is enlarged.
And similarly, if the opening is wide, then you should approximate the edges with sutures and leave it in a quantity sufficient for the irrigation to be added.
And if the opening from which the flow comes is raised to the upper parts, then dry it in the lower part where the flow runs below, for when the arm is constricted at the depth of the sinus, flesh will be generated there.
And if it is not possible to dry the sinus within the lower part of the bone as you wish, then prepare the member with a preparation so that the flow runs lightly according to your convenience and without any obstruction hindering the flow.
Move what is above the opening of the sinus, which you should probe at all times so that what is lodged in it may come out. And so that you may know whether what comes from the wound of the arm is thick or thin, or whether it is digested or undigested.
And in this way you should consider the location of that sinus, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and whether it is in the abscess.
And as your treatment is prolonged in this manner, and you see that the matter deposited over the opening of the sinus has adhered or will adhere, then you should loosen it on the first day or every third day, and when you loosen the crust, then change the cloth for another and renew the dressing.
But if within the sinus there is empty space where subtle pus is present, then do not despair of its adherence, for healing of it is appropriate, as in some people the generation of flesh in their wounds is slow, and in others the opposite occurs.
And if for many days the wound is indigest and pus is not flowing from the sinus, then you know that the sinus does not adhere; and if the adherence of the sinus is delayed and this causes prolongation, then adjust to drying properties of the medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and in their virtue, they should be dried as well when applied as a dressing, especially when there is an excess of moisture.
And the most important thing in curing it is to take a finely prepared dressing and dissolve it in rose oil, and apply it over what has been previously treated with an ointment of its substance, and use this as needed.
In that action, when there is no bandage, find a dressing, and use honey which has been cooked to thicken it; or take myrrh and aloes and mix them, then sprinkle all over the honey which is on the fire and immediately spread linen over cloth and stretch that over the wound; and apply that with the honey which you have cooked until it thickens, and sprinkle over cloth and stretch that.

And if the wound is prolonged and has not been healed by this treatment, then you know that corruption is in its root, and it makes an inquiry into the bones or other hard members or ligaments; now treat it with fistula treatment as mentioned above.
On the treatment of boil wounds, worn nails, and the cutting of an added finger and sectioning.
A boil is an abscess that arises from under the nail of a toe or finger of the hand or foot, and sometimes it appears on other fingers. As it prolongs and its treatment is delayed, it can become an abscess caused by cautery, or it may be corrupted. It generates pus inside which corrodes the root of the nail, and very quickly corrupts the entire area, spreading its corruption to the bone causing a foul odor. The extremity of the finger becomes disfigured, and its color turns dark.
And when you have that as we said in the division and do not find your treatment effective, then it is necessary for you to incise with a scalpel all the excess that is rotten from the nail and immediately cauterize the wound nearby, because cauterization is beneficial in such cases.
If the bone is sound and the tendon is healthy, and the divisions of the tendon are already healed to their respective parts, they begin to pierce and irritate that area. Now you should take a fine needle and place it at the angle of the tendon where you will puncture the flesh, then push it upwards and cut through that flesh easily; pause over what remains of the flesh with medicines that corrode and burn until it is completely consumed; and afterwards treat that wound with remedies until it is healed.
If the corruption has already spread to the bone, now you should cut out that part of the bone and extract it, because it will never heal as long as the bone remains corrupted.
And if you see the corrosion and corruption spreading to the digit, now you should cut out that part at one of its joints according to where it is necessary, and then treat it until it is healed.
If there is an injury or inflammation in the tendon, and there is severe pain there, now you should bleed the patient at the beginning, and then dry out the tendon with a sharp spatula across its surface from top to bottom, but be careful that the incision does not penetrate into the flesh below the tendon, for you would cause intense pain to the patient, and it would lead to the excessive growth of new tissue in that location; and afterwards treat that area with something that relieves pain.
But the condition that arises in most people is that it becomes excessively fleshy very easily, or there is little bone, or it affects the tendon very easily.
And some of them arise at the root of the joint, or the growth occurs in some of the joints of the tendons. He who is born with weak joints of the fingers will not suffer much, and he who is born with strong joints in the limbs will be less troubled.
And for those who are born with fleshy bodies, the operation will be easier, and you should cauterize that part with a hot iron spatula.
But for one who is born with a condition at the joint, the cure is difficult; therefore, guard against its amputation.
But for one who is born with weak fingers, you should cauterize the flesh at the beginning with a round cauterization down to the bone, and then use one of those appropriate saws to cut, and subsequently treat what remains until it heals.
But for consolidation that occurs between the bones due to injury or because of the person's birth condition, or due to healing from an illness or burning by fire, or similarly, then you should operate on that consolidation until the said parts return to their natural form.
And then place between the bandages soaked in rose oil so that they do not heal too quickly, and separate them, or place between them a thin sheet of lead until it is properly healed.
And similarly, if consolidation occurs in any of the bones on the palm, then you should treat that consolidation according to how it is prepared and appropriate to the figure of the limb.
Of cauterization for veins, these are varicose veins.
Veins that are varicose are those wrapped thickly and full of melancholic humors, which move in the limbs of the body, and they most commonly occur in the legs, especially in the legs of travelers, workers, and carriers.
Then you should administer purgatives for the black bile several times with strong expulsion, and subsequently bleed the patient from the basilic vein.
The treatment of their condition with iron is according to two methods: one is that it should be incised and the black blood drawn out, and the other method is that the vein should be raised and all of it extracted.
The sectioning of it is according to this method: at the beginning, apply a poultice with hot water until the thick blood is dissolved, which will be sediment in the poultice, and then press the poultice on the patient's body at the most prominent part inside at the lower part of the navel with a bandage, and then dry the vein in one place, or two, or three with wide sectioning, and then draw out the black blood with the right hand from below the poultice upwards inside until the quantity is removed that you want and that suffices for what the patient can tolerate.
And then advise him, and command him to abstain from foods that generate black bile.
And repeat the treatment by phlebotomy when the veins are full, and note this to the patient.

For the operation to open an ulcer, use hooks and scrape away the vein from all parts until it appears to the touch, and when you see that part where it turns black, you should expose it.
And thus when you open it, and of the ulcer you see that white which is its core.

On cutting into worms generated under the skin and it is called bovine illness.

On incision for inflammation of the throat.
This illness is called in our land nafir, and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs, and it often changes from one limb to another.
And now I will describe that as I shall recount to you. I was called to attend to a sick woman in a village, and when I uncovered her arm, I saw a small inflammation in the funis vein of the arm. After waiting for about an hour, I observed that this inflammation spreading gradually, as if it were quicksilver moving from place to place, though more quickly than could be expected.
And then the pain moved from that location to the muscle, and it remained there for about an hour.
And then it moved to the other side of the body until it reached the other arm.
And then she told me that it was moving throughout her body as I had observed, and I was greatly amazed by the change and the speed with which it moved from limb to limb. And I had seen something similar before in my own patients in that manner, but I have never witnessed such pain changing from limb to limb. But I did not see this in my patients as I did in the woman.
And I did not think this could be anything other than the result of her being weak, with a dual nature and exposed veins, in which such airiness and changing sensations appear.
It is necessary that there does not appear according to this back-curling in those who are delicate and whose flesh is moist from burst veins.
And when you want the treatment for it, and the patient feels that pain, at that time it is not apparent as we have said; then you press firmly on that area and leave it briefly so that the trapped air can escape, and cauterize the spot.
But if you do not perform it with your hands, then treat that by inducing sweating and by expelling air, and apply plasters for foul-smelling pills and for senna pills and similar remedies.
Of the extraction of thorns.
Thorns are diverse according to their species and the parts of the body where they lodge, for their diversity is that some have large points, others small, some concave, others blunt; and they may be solid. There are also those with three angles, and those with tongues; and there are rod-like ones.
And the signs of a headache are when it seizes in the sagitta, and passes through the bone, and exits from the cephalus which is above the brain, for there occurs by the soda vehement, and scotomia, and vertigo, and rigor in the eyes, and inflammation and rigor of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding and vomiting of bile, and easily speech is cut off and the voice is destroyed, and from the place of the ailment comes out white moisture like dust, and there comes about dryness of the face as with the wetness of flesh.
And so if these signs appear to you, then you must abstain from treatment and the extraction of the arrow, unless it is outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it strikes in the heart, so that it is near the left mamilla, and feel there where it has been driven into a hard place, and not into a soft place; and easily the movement of the arrow is like the movement of the pulse, and blood from the wound is black, and dryness comes over those extremities, and cold sweat appears, and fainting occurs; therefore you know that death will come very soon.
And the signs when the arrow has struck the lung are that blood with foam comes from the wound, and the veins near the neck become swollen, and the complexion changes, and great breath is exhaled, and there is a craving for cold air.
And if the arrow strikes in the vena cava which is in the chest, and then the pain is near the small ribs, and there is great difficulty and severe pain and much sighing, and it does not allow movement of all the limbs by the muscles.
And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, immediately apply remedies for the plague and any indigestible food.
And if the arrow strikes in the abdomen and is embedded within it, apply a poultice for the plague, or use cloth or gut ligatures where it is severed, and there is no hope for recovery by extracting the arrow.
And if the arrow strikes in the bladder and urine comes out with it, and the process causes some injury to the surrounding parts, and there is severe pain over the wound, then you know that it is fatal.
But in other members as well, such as the face, the neck, and the jaw, the shoulders, and the helpers [muscles], and the vertebrae of the back, and the clavicle, and the ribs and similar parts of the limbs, they are saved according to the best dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery and is not a venomous arrow.
And I recount this to you as I have seen regarding the nature of these arrows, so that it may signify to you concerning your own treatment.
The cause is that when an arrow struck a man in the lacrimal bone near the root of his nose, I extracted it from the other side and left the bones of his ear intact, and he healed without any harm coming to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew, which had struck him in the bone of his eye, leaving the eyelid intact. The arrow was deeply embedded and could only be obtained with a small part to which it adhered; it was a large sharp arrow of those used by the Turks, made of iron like a lion's tooth, without any notches.
This is from the Cæsarea, and no ill accident happens in its vicinity.
And I extracted an arrow from a Christian man who was injured in the groin, and it was an Arabian arrow, and it had penetrated deep into his body; then I incised around that area between two grooves, and then I delicately removed that arrow, and the Christian man recovered.
And I extracted an arrow from a man who was struck in his abdomen, and he seemed likely to die because of it; however, after thirty days had passed and there was no change in his condition, I incised around the arrow and worked on it, and he recovered, and no further ill accident happened to him.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow had struck both sides of him, and the wound had become consolidated on him, and after seven years had passed, I extracted the arrow from the root of the wound.
And I saw a woman in whom an arrow had struck her abdomen, and the wound had become consolidated inside her, and there was no change in her condition over time, and the woman did not experience any difficulty with her natural functions.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow had struck his face, and the wound had become consolidated, and he broke the arrow without feeling any pain, and many similar cases are like this.

Chapter One.
Summary and collection from the treatment of fractures of bones, from those whose preliminaries are necessary before we begin the remembrance of the members of fractures and various things pertaining to each. Therefore, let us say in the prologue of this chapter the summaries of the speech; and the chapters to which one must pay attention at the beginning for understanding are necessary for the craftsman and to stand on the truth of those; so that you and those who wish to know or learn this noble art may do so quickly.
And therefore I say that when it happens to someone to suffer a fracture or dislocation or twist or fall, at that moment you must consider at the beginning whether to perform venesection or to bandage them, or both together, if no cause prohibits it, such as weakness of strength, or it is a child to whom it happens, or an elderly person in decrepitude, or it is a time of extreme heat or cold.
And then be content with food such as fresh herbs and the meat of birds and small game; and avoid fatty meats and foods that fill the body, including any food that fills the veins with blood, until you are sure that there is no risk of an abscess forming, and if you do not fear an effusion of matter into the limb.
Then return the patient to his usual regimen as he was accustomed before.
And when the broken bone begins to be restored, it is then necessary that the patient be fed with nutritious foods consisting of meat and heavy items, as well as viscous foods such as those made from wheat boiled with water, rice, peas, cattle stomachs, eggs, fresh cheese, and strong wine similar to these. And with this regimen, the coagulation of the fracture occurs more easily and better.
And know that bones broken in humans during the first stage and in the elderly cannot be continued and consolidated according to their nature by drying of the limbs.
But nature adjusts and applies to the broken bone from all parts some cause similar to glue, in which there is a thickness that adheres and strengthens it within what is conglutinated and joined together, until they come to their end of strength and firmness, just as fire at the beginning, and no cause prevents them from performing their works.
And for this reason it is necessary to restrict the patient's diet to foods that are heavy and viscous and thick, as we have said.
And know that the types of fractures are diverse according to the diversity of the limbs, for a fracture of the bone in the hand is different from a fracture of the skull bone; and a fracture of the foot bone is different from a fracture of the rib bone; and similarly all other members differ among themselves.
